<div class="ltx_abstract">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_title_abstract">Abstract</h6>
<p class="ltx_p">We calculate models of stellar evolution for very massive stars and include the effects of modified gravity to investigate the influence on the physical properties of blue supergiant stars and their use as extragalactic distance indicators. With shielding and fifth force parameters in a similar range as in previous studies of Cepheid and tip of the red giant branch (TRGB) stars we find clear effects on stellar luminosity and flux-weighted gravity. The relationship between flux weighted gravity, <span id="m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span id="m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\equiv"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">≡</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> g/<span id="m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="T_{\mathrm{eff}}^{4}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.12em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.12em;">T</span></span></span><span class="mjx-stack" style="vertical-align: -0.343em;"><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-bottom: 0.255em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, and bolometric magnitude <span id="m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\mathrm{bol}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.219em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">b</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">o</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">l</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;(FGLR), which has been used successfully for accurate distance determinations, is systematically affected. While the stellar evolution FGLRs show a systematic offset from the observed relation, we can use the differential shifts between models with Newtonian and modified gravity to estimate the influence on FGLR distance determinations. Modified gravity leads to a distance increase of 0.05 to 0.15 magnitudes in distance modulus. These change are comparable to the ones found for Cepheid stars. We compare observed FGLR and TRGB distances of nine galaxies to constrain the free parameters of modified gravity. Not accounting for systematic differences between TRGB and FGLR distances shielding parameters of 5<span id="m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and fifth force parameters of 1/3 and 1 can be ruled out with about 90% confidence. Allowing for potential systematic offsets between TRGB and FGLR distances no determination is possible for a shielding parameter of 10<span id="m8" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. For 5<span id="m9" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="m10" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> a fifth force parameter of 1 can be ruled out to 92% but 1/3 is unlikely only to 60%.</p>

<div class="ltx_keywords">gravitation - stars: fundamental parameters, luminosity
</div>
<span class="ltx_note ltx_role_journal"><sup class="ltx_note_mark">†</sup><span class="ltx_note_outer"><span class="ltx_note_content"><sup class="ltx_note_mark">†</sup><span class="ltx_note_type">journal: </span>ApJ</span></span></span>
<section id="S1" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">1 </span>Introduction</h2>

<div id="S1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The discovery of dark matter and of the accelerated expansion of the universe has triggered a substantial amount of approaches to explain these revolutionary astronomical discoveries by a modification of general relativity. These approaches introduce a new scalar degree of freedom in scalar-tensor theories coupling to ordinary matter and lead to a fifth force which changes gravitational attraction. Most promising are concepts which include a screening mechanism where the new force is suppressed in deep potential wells or regions of high density but influences gravity outside these regions. A prominent example of this class of models are the ones discussed by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Khoury and Weltman (<a href="#bib.bib193" title="Chameleon cosmology" class="ltx_ref">2004</a>)</cite> and <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Brax<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib194" title="Detecting dark energy in orbit: The cosmological chameleon" class="ltx_ref">2004</a>)</cite>, where a non-linear screening of a scalar field, a so called chameleon field, can suppress modifications of gravity on galactic scales. For an introduction and overview we refer to <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Chang and Hui (<a href="#bib.bib177" title="Stellar Structure and Tests of Modified Gravity" class="ltx_ref">2011</a>); Davis<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib178" title="Modified gravity makes galaxies brighter" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>); Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>); Desmond<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib181" title="Local resolution of the Hubble tension: The impact of screened fifth forces on the cosmic distance ladder" class="ltx_ref">2019</a>); Sakstein (<a href="#bib.bib179" title="Astrophysical Tests of Screened Modified Gravity" class="ltx_ref">2020</a>)</cite>. In the case of massive galaxies or of dwarf galaxies in the neighborhood of massive galaxies the potential wells will shield the stars against the fifth force (see <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Cabré<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib190" title="Astrophysical tests of gravity: a screening map of the nearby universe" class="ltx_ref">2012</a></cite> for a detailed description), but for isolated smaller galaxies modified gravity may affect the internal structure of stars through a modification of the equation of hydrostatic equilibrium resulting in changes of observational stellar properties such as luminosity, temperature, radius and pulsation periods. Most promising are evolved stars, giants or supergiants, because their envelopes may be unscreened against the fifth force due to their large radii and the resulting lower gravitational potential.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> systematically investigated two types of evolved stars, low mass stars at the tip of the red giant branch (TRGB) and massive Cepheid stars of 5 to 10 <span id="S1.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;in the stellar instability strip. They found that both the luminosity of TRGB stars and the period-luminosity relationship of Cepheids are affected. As a result, extragalactic distances obtained from these objects are altered, most interestingly in opposite direction, as TRGB distances decrease due to a decreased luminosity (see also <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Desmond and Sakstein <a href="#bib.bib180" title="Screened fifth forces lower the TRGB-calibrated Hubble constant too" class="ltx_ref">2020</a></cite>), whereas Cepheid distances increase because of the decrease of pulsation period. Comparing with observed galaxy distances <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> obtained constraints on the potential scalar background field.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Blue supergiant stars provide an important alternative to Cepheids as distance indicators through their relationship between flux-weighted gravity and luminosity <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib20" title="A New Extragalactic Distance Determination Method Using the Flux-weighted Gravity of Late B and Early A Supergiants" class="ltx_ref">2003</a>, <a href="#bib.bib6" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of 24 A Supergiants in the Sculptor Galaxy NGC 300: Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship, Metallicity, and Metallicity Gradient" class="ltx_ref">2008</a>; Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib46" title="LMC Blue Supergiant Stars and the Calibration of the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship" class="ltx_ref">2017</a>)</cite>. They have higher masses than Cepheids and are significantly more luminous with substantially larger radii. The gravitational potential of their envelopes is comparable to the one of Cepheids and, consequently, effects of modified gravity may be equally important. We have therefore carried out stellar evolution calculations for massive stars in the range from 12 to 60 <span id="S1.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;to investigate how modified gravity influences the observable stellar properties and whether it introduces detectable systematic changes to the flux-weighted gravity - luminosity relationship (FGLR).
</p>
</div>
<figure id="S1.F1" class="ltx_figure"><img src="x1.png" id="S1.F1.g1" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering" width="319" height="319" alt="
The observed FGLR of blue supergiant stars in the LMC (see text).
">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 1: </span>
The observed FGLR of blue supergiant stars in the LMC (see text).
</figcaption>
</figure>
</section>
<section id="S2" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">2 </span>Flux-weighted Gravity- Luminosity Relationship (FGLR)</h2>

<div id="S2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Blue supergiant stars (BSG) are massive stars in the temperature range 7900K <span id="S2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\leq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <span id="S2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="T_{\mathrm{eff}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.12em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.12em;">T</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.23em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">e</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span id="S2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\leq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 25000K (see <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib46" title="LMC Blue Supergiant Stars and the Calibration of the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship" class="ltx_ref">2017</a></cite>). Their tight observational relationship between absolute stellar magnitude <span id="S2.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\mathrm{bol}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.219em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">b</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">o</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">l</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;and flux weighted gravity <span id="S2.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, <span id="S2.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;= <span id="S2.p1.m7" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log\,g"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.167em; height: 0px;"></span><span class="mjx-mi MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;- 4log(<span id="S2.p1.m8" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="T_{\mathrm{eff}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.12em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.12em;">T</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.23em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">e</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>/10<span id="S2.p1.m9" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{4}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">4</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>K), has been discovered by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib20" title="A New Extragalactic Distance Determination Method Using the Flux-weighted Gravity of Late B and Early A Supergiants" class="ltx_ref">2003</a>)</cite>. It is a simple consequence of the well known power law relationship between stellar luminosity and mass and the fact the massive stars evolve from their hydrogen burning main sequence to the red supergiant phase at almost constant luminosity. With absolute visual magnitudes up to -10 mag BSG are beacons in the universe and much brighter than other stellar distance indicators such as Cepheids or TRGB stars. This allows for spectroscopic studies out to distances of 10 Mpc with present day telescopes and a factor four further out with the next generation of 30m to 40m ground based telescopes. In consequence, the FGLR has a great potential for extragalactic distance determinations. <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib6" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of 24 A Supergiants in the Sculptor Galaxy NGC 300: Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship, Metallicity, and Metallicity Gradient" class="ltx_ref">2008</a>)</cite> studying a large sample of BSG in the sculptor galaxy NGC 300 have provided a first calibration of the FGLR and subsequently distances to eight galaxies have been determined: WLM – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib23" title="The Araucaria Project: The Local Group Galaxy WLM\mdashDistance and Metallicity from Quantitative Spectroscopy of Blue Supergiants" class="ltx_ref">2008</a>)</cite>; M33 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">U<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib38" title="A New Distance to M33 Using Blue Supergiants and the FGLR Method" class="ltx_ref">2009</a>)</cite>; M81 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib34" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of Blue Supergiant Stars in the Disk of M81: Metallicity, Metallicity Gradient, and Distance" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>)</cite>; NGC3109 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Hosek<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib4" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of Blue Supergiants in Metal-poor Dwarf Galaxy NGC 3109" class="ltx_ref">2014</a>)</cite>; NGC3621 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib35" title="Stellar Metallicity of the Extended Disk and Distance of the Spiral Galaxy NGC 3621" class="ltx_ref">2014</a>)</cite>; M83 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Bresolin<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib12" title="Young Stars and Ionized Nebulae in M83: Comparing Chemical Abundances at High Metallicity." class="ltx_ref">2016</a>)</cite>; NGC55 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib5" title="A Spectroscopic Study of Blue Supergiant Stars in the Sculptor Galaxy NGC 55: Chemical Evolution and Distance" class="ltx_ref">2016</a>)</cite>; IC1613 – <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Berger<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib184" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of Supergiants in the Local Group Dwarf Galaxy IC 1613: Metallicity and Distance" class="ltx_ref">2018</a>)</cite>. We note that these galaxies cover a wide range of stellar metallicities from about 1/10 solar to twice solar but no significant metallicity dependence of the FGLR has been found. These observational findings are in agreement with stellar evolution calculations which also show that the effects of metallicity on the FGLR are small <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Meynet<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib52" title="The flux-weighted gravity-luminosity relationship of blue supergiant stars as a constraint for stellar evolution" class="ltx_ref">2015</a>)</cite>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The most recent calibration of the FGLR is given by the work of <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib46" title="LMC Blue Supergiant Stars and the Calibration of the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship" class="ltx_ref">2017</a>)</cite>. They carried out a detailed quantitative spectroscopic NLTE analysis of 90 BSG in the LMC and determined stellar effective temperatures, gravities and element abundances. Figure <a href="#S1.F1" title="Figure 1 ‣ 1 Introduction ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a> shows the FGLR resulting from their work. The 2-component regression fit to the data provides the new calibration, which is given by</p>

<div id="S2.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We note that our Figure <a href="#S1.F1" title="Figure 1 ‣ 1 Introduction ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a> and the value of b in eqn. (1) are slightly different from the original results obtained by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib46" title="LMC Blue Supergiant Stars and the Calibration of the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship" class="ltx_ref">2017</a>)</cite>, since we now use the 1 percent precision distance to the LMC determined by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Pietrzyński<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib56" title="A distance to the Large Magellanic Cloud that is precise to one per cent" class="ltx_ref">2019</a>)</cite> from the light curve and radial velocity analysis of 20 late type eclipsing binaries and an improved stellar surface brightness-color relationship.</p>

</section>
<section id="S3" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">3 </span>Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution</h2>

<div id="S3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The effects of modified gravity on stellar structure depend on two free parameters, the self-screening parameter <span id="S3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and the fifth force parameter <span id="S3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> (see <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a></cite>). <span id="S3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> describes how efficient a star is screening itself against the fifth force. It is used to determine the screening radius r<span id="S3.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> inside the star through the condition</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<div class="ltx_engrafo_equation_container"><table id="S3.E4" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><span id="S3.E4.m1" class="ltx_DisplayMath"><span class="mjpage mjpage__block"><span class="mjx-chtml MJXc-display" style="text-align: left;"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label=" \chi_{c}={4\pi\over c^{2}}G_{0}\int_{r_{s}}^{R}r\rho(r)dr, "><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mo MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.077em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">=</span></span><span class="mjx-texatom MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 1.273em; padding: 0px 0.12em;"><span class="mjx-numerator" style="width: 1.273em; top: -1.379em;"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">4</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.003em;">π</span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-denominator" style="width: 1.273em; vertical-align: 0.409em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="border-bottom: 1.3px solid; top: -0.296em; width: 1.273em;" class="mjx-line"></span></span><span style="height: 2.232em; vertical-align: -0.854em;" class="mjx-vsize"></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">G</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.388em;"><span class="mjx-mo" style="vertical-align: 0.001em; padding-right: 0.388em;"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-size2-R" style="padding-top: 1.109em; padding-bottom: 1.109em;">∫</span></span></span><span class="mjx-stack" style="vertical-align: -0.921em;"><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-bottom: 2.364em; padding-left: 0.784em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.593em;">(</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">r</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">r</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="margin-top: -0.144em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">,</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(4)</span></td>
</tr>
</tbody></table></div>
</div>
<div id="S3.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">where r is the radial coordinate inside the star, R the stellar radius, G<span id="S3.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> the Newtonian gravitational constant and c the speed of light. Inside the screening radius the fifth force is screened and only Newtonian gravity with G<span id="S3.p3.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is acting. <span id="S3.p3.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\rho(r)"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">ρ</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.593em;">(</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">r</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.593em;">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is the density profile of the star. Exterior to r<span id="S3.p3.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> the fifth force contributes and leads to a radius dependent gravitation via</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p4" class="ltx_para">
<div class="ltx_engrafo_equation_container"><table id="S3.E5" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">G</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; </tbody></table></div>
</div>
<div id="S3.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span id="S3.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> sets the maximum contribution of the fifth force. M(r) and M(r<span id="S3.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>) correspond to the stellar mass enclosed inside the radius r and the screening radius r<span id="S3.p5.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, respectively.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For the physics of stellar structure and evolution the implementation of modified gravity through eqns. (4) and (5) is straightforward through a replacement of G<span id="S3.p6.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> by G(r) in the equation of hydrostatic equilibrium as demonstrated in the work by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Chang and Hui (<a href="#bib.bib177" title="Stellar Structure and Tests of Modified Gravity" class="ltx_ref">2011</a>); Davis<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib178" title="Modified gravity makes galaxies brighter" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>); Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite>. For main sequence stars, analytical estimates of the main effects can easily be obtained. For instance, using the well know mass-luminosity relation (see eq. 6 below) it is straightforward to show that stellar luminosity increases as a consequence of the rise from G<span id="S3.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to G(r). For advanced stages of stellar evolution such as Cepheids and red giants stars numerical models are needed in conjunction with analytical considerations.
</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The case of massive BSG is more complex, because their evolution is complicated by the effects of strong stellar winds and rapid rotation. Thus, to investigate the influence of modified gravity requires the detailed use of numerical models. For our study we have used the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">MESA</span> stellar evolution code version 12115 <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Paxton<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib89" title="Modules for Experiments in Stellar Astrophysics (MESA)" class="ltx_ref">2011</a>, <a href="#bib.bib90" title="Modules for Experiments in Stellar Astrophysics (MESA): Planets, Oscillations, Rotation, and Massive Stars" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>, <a href="#bib.bib91" title="Modules for Experiments in Stellar Astrophysics (MESA): Binaries, Pulsations, and Explosions" class="ltx_ref">2015</a>, <a href="#bib.bib92" title="Modules for Experiments in Stellar Astrophysics (MESA): Convective Boundaries, Element Diffusion, and Massive Star Explosions" class="ltx_ref">2018</a>, <a href="#bib.bib93" title="Modules for Experiments in Stellar Astrophysics (MESA): Pulsating Variable Stars, Rotation, Convective Boundaries, and Energy Conservation" class="ltx_ref">2019</a>)</cite>. One of the many advantages of <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">MESA</span> is that it provides a simple way to override most of physical routines without modifying more than one file. Since <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">MESA</span> already has a variable that holds the value of the gravitational constant for each radial cell in the star, the implication of modified gravity for a given pair of values <span id="S3.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span id="S3.p7.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is simple. All it requires is a numerical determination of the screening radius r<span id="S3.p7.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and then the values of G<span id="S3.p7.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> are replaced by G(r) outside the screening radius in all equations, which contain G. This approach has already been used by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Chang and Hui (<a href="#bib.bib177" title="Stellar Structure and Tests of Modified Gravity" class="ltx_ref">2011</a>); Davis<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib178" title="Modified gravity makes galaxies brighter" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>); Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For our numerical calculations of BSG evolution using <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">MESA</span> we adopt Z = 0.0067 for the metallicity mass fraction corresponding to the average metallicity of the 90 BSG in the LMC determined by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib46" title="LMC Blue Supergiant Stars and the Calibration of the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship" class="ltx_ref">2017</a>)</cite>. For the effects of mass-loss we apply the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">MESA</span> module, which uses the results obtained by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Vink<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib94" title="On the nature of the bi-stability jump in the winds of early-type supergiants" class="ltx_ref">1999</a>, <a href="#bib.bib95" title="New theoretical mass-loss rates of O and B stars" class="ltx_ref">2000</a>, <a href="#bib.bib96" title="Mass-loss predictions for O and B stars as a function of metallicity" class="ltx_ref">2001</a>)</cite> based on the theory of radiation driven winds (see <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki and Puls <a href="#bib.bib1" title="Winds from Hot Stars" class="ltx_ref">2000</a></cite>). For internal stellar layers with convection a mixing length parameter <span id="S3.p8.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{\rm MLT}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">M</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">L</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">T</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1.6 and step function overshooting with an overshooting parameter <span id="S3.p8.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{\rm OV}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.23em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">O</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">V</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 0.1 are used. Our models include stellar rotation with initial rotational velocities on the zero-age-main-sequence as in <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Ekström<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib109" title="Grids of stellar models with rotation. I. Models from 0.8 to 120 M☉ at solar metallicity (Z = 0.014)" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>)</cite> and they also account for rotationally enhanced mass-loss. Eddington-Sweet circulation (with Eddington Sweet factor 0.5) instability, Goldreich-Schubert-Fricke instability, Solberg-Hoiland instability and secular shear instability <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Heger<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib105" title="Presupernova Evolution of Rotating Massive Stars. I. Numerical Method and Evolution of the Internal Stellar Structure" class="ltx_ref">2000</a>)</cite> induced by rotation and resulting in mixing are also included.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For our investigation we calculate a grid of evolutionary models with initial masses of 12, 13, 15, 18, 20, 23, 25, 29, 32, 37, 40, 43, 45, 50, 60 <span id="S3.p9.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>, respectively. To check our adaption of the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">MESA</span> code we also compare in detail with the comprehensive sets of the Newtonian state-of-the-art stellar evolution models by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Ekström<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib109" title="Grids of stellar models with rotation. I. Models from 0.8 to 120 M☉ at solar metallicity (Z = 0.014)" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>)</cite> and <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Georgy<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib53" title="Grids of stellar models with rotation. III. Models from 0.8 to 120 Msun at a metallicity Z = 0.002" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite>. For this comparison we adjust our metallity to their values (Milky Way and Small Magellanic Cloud metallicities, respectively). We find good agreement over the whole mass range.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p10" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For the selection of the modified gravity parameters <span id="S3.p10.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span id="S3.p10.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> we use the work by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> as guideline. <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> discussed self-shielding parameters <span id="S3.p10.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> in a range from 10<span id="S3.p10.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to 10<span id="S3.p10.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and fifth force parameters <span id="S3.p10.m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> in a range from 0.2 to 1 with special emphasis on models with <span id="S3.p10.m7" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3 and 1. Comparing observed galaxy distances determined from Cepheid and TRGB stars they concluded that for <span id="S3.p10.m8" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3 values of <span id="S3.p10.m9" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}\geqq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mo MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-ams-R" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≧</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 5<span id="S3.p10.m10" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S3.p10.m11" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> can be ruled out with 95% confidence. For <span id="S3.p10.m12" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1 values of <span id="S3.p10.m13" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}\geqq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mo MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-ams-R" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≧</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 1<span id="S3.p10.m14" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S3.p10.m15" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> can be ruled out with similar evidence. Following this discussion we select <span id="S3.p10.m16" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5<span id="S3.p10.m17" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S3.p10.m18" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and 10<span id="S3.p10.m19" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span id="S3.p10.m20" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3 and 1, respectively, and compare with models which do not include modified gravity. We note that <span id="S3.p10.m21" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}=1/3"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mo MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.077em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">=</span></span><span class="mjx-mn MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">1</span></span><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.593em;">/</span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">3</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> corresponds to models with non-linear terms in gravity sector of the Lagrangian, i.e. so called <span id="S3.p10.m22" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="f(R)"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.06em;">f</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.593em;">(</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">R</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.593em;">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> theories, as for example explored as inflationary scenario by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Starobinsky (<a href="#bib.bib196" title="A new type of isotropic cosmological models without singularity" class="ltx_ref">1980</a>)</cite> or in the context of dark energy by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Hu and Sawicki (<a href="#bib.bib197" title="Models of f(R) cosmic acceleration that evade solar system tests" class="ltx_ref">2007</a>)</cite> or additional spatial dimensions <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Dvali<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib195" title="4D gravity on a brane in 5D Minkowski space" class="ltx_ref">2000</a>)</cite>, albeit the screening mechanism in the latter is the Vainshtein mechanism <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Vainshtein <a href="#bib.bib198" title="To the problem of nonvanishing gravitation mass" class="ltx_ref">1972</a>)</cite>. We should additionally note that a recent analysis by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Desmond and Ferreira (<a href="#bib.bib182" title="Galaxy morphology rules out astrophysically relevant Hu-Sawicki f (R ) gravity" class="ltx_ref">2020</a>)</cite>, who investigated the constraints on modified gravity from a statistical study of galaxy morphology, seems to rule out Hu-Sawacki f(R) gravity.</p>
