<div id="S3.p11" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Figure <a href="#S3.F2" title="Figure 2 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a> shows the classical Hertzsprung-Russell diagram (HRD) of the evolutionary tracks for both cases, Newtonian and modified gravity. As we can see, modified gravity increases the luminosity of massive stars. The effect increases with screening parameter <span id="S3.p11.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and fifth force parameter <span id="S3.p11.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. This effect is a simple consequence of the change from G<span id="S3.p11.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to G(r) as described by equation (5).</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p12" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">As is well known (see, for instance, <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kippenhahn<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib185" title="Stellar Structure and Evolution" class="ltx_ref">2012</a></cite> or <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Davis<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib178" title="Modified gravity makes galaxies brighter" class="ltx_ref">2012</a></cite>), a simple estimate of the relationship between stellar luminosity and stellar mass for stars on the main sequence yields</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p13" class="ltx_para">
<div class="ltx_engrafo_equation_container"><table id="S3.E6" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><span id="S3.E6.m1" class="ltx_DisplayMath"><span class="mjpage mjpage__block"><span class="mjx-chtml MJXc-display" style="text-align: left;"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label=" L\propto G^{4}M^{3}. "><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">L</span></span><span class="mjx-mo MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">∝</span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">G</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.584em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">4</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.584em; padding-left: 0.22em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">3</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="margin-top: -0.144em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(6)</span></td>
</tr>
</tbody></table></div>
</div>
<div id="S3.p14" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We note that in our range of stellar masses the exponent of M is slightly smaller, 2.5 instead of 3, because of the influence of radiation pressure which increases with increasing stellar mass. We also note from Figure <a href="#S3.F2" title="Figure 2 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a> that BSG follow a similar relationship except that the luminosities are about a factor of ten larger than on the main sequence. Therefore, if the screening radius is located deep inside the massive stars, they should experience the increase from G<span id="S3.p14.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to G(r) and become more luminous. In the following we discuss this more quantitatively. We introduce an analytical fit of the density stratification inside massive stars during their evolution and and use this to derive an approximation for the location of the screening radius as a function of stellar parameters.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p15" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The density distribution of a massive star on the main sequence is reasonably well approximated by adopting constant density inside the stellar core r<span id="S3.p15.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and an exponential decline with scale height H outside the stellar core:</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p16" class="ltx_para">
<div class="ltx_engrafo_equation_container"><table id="S3.E7" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<div id="S3.p21" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Figure <a href="#S3.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> displays an example for the density distribution fit of a 15 <span id="S3.p21.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;star at the zero-age-mains-sequence (ZAMS). While the fit is not perfect, in particular above r/R <span id="S3.p21.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\sim"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.077em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">∼</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 0.9, it is good enough for the discussion of the effects of modified gravity, as we will explain below. We use <span id="S3.p21.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\delta_{ms}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.007em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.007em;">δ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">m</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 0.08 and <span id="S3.p21.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="f_{\delta}^{ms}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.06em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.06em;">f</span></span></span><span class="mjx-stack" style="vertical-align: -0.351em;"><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-bottom: 0.255em; padding-left: 0.181em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">m</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.007em;">δ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 2.5 for the main sequence density fits.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p22" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">During the evolution away from the main sequence into the BSG phase the density distribution changes dramatically. The stellar core contracts and the outer layers expand. As a result, the density increases strongly in a small central volume, while it decreases for the rest of the star. Figure <a href="#S3.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> shows the example of 15 <span id="S3.p22.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;star at the end of BSG phase at <span id="S3.p22.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="T_{\mathrm{eff}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.12em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.12em;">T</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.23em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">e</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>= 7900K. A simple analytical fit is</p>
</div>

<div id="S3.p28" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We apply <span id="S3.p28.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\delta_{bsg}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.007em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.007em;">δ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.219em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">b</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 0.06 as the best fit to describe the exponential decline outside the stellar core.
For the mass M<span id="S3.p28.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> confined in the contracted central core we use the core mass of the ZAMS phase defined as</p>

<div id="S3.p30" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">where R<span id="S3.p30.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{ms}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">m</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is the stellar radius on the ZAMS. With R the actual stellar radius in the BSG phase we then adopt</p>

<div id="S3.p32" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">which means that the core radius r<span id="S3.p32.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> in the BSG phase is one fifth of the core radius on the ZAMS taking into account the contraction of the stellar core. This leads to the simple relationship between the central densities of the ZAMS and BSG phases</p>
</div>

</figcaption>
</figure>
<div id="S3.p34" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The analytical fit obtained in this way is not excellent but to zero order captures the development of the density distribution during the evolution to the BSG phase well.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p35" class="ltx_para">

<div id="S3.p39" class="ltx_para">

padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>e<span id="S3.p39.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{r_{c}\over H}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.744em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 0.945em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.057em;">H</span></span></span><span style="border-bottom: 1px solid; top: -0.296em; width: 0.945em;" class="mjx-line"></span></span><span style="height: 1.608em; vertical-align: -0.588em;" class="mjx-vsize"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> for the ZAMS and to <span id="S3.p39.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\rho_{i}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">i</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> in the BSG phase, respectively. For R and <span id="S3.p39.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\delta"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.007em;">δ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> we select the corresponding ZAMS and BSG values.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p40" class="ltx_para">

<p class="ltx_p">drops below the chameleon threshold for screening <span id="S3.p40.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>.
Figure <a href="#S3.F4" title="Figure 4 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> shows the function <span id="S3.p40.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> of eqn. (20) versus r/R for the two examples of Figure <a href="#S3.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> and compares with the analytical approximation.
We see that for radii r/R <span id="S3.p40.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\leqq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-ams-R" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≦</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 0.8 the failure of the analytical density approximation in the main sequence case (left part of Figure <a href="#S3.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a>) has only a small influence on the analytical approximation of <span id="S3.p40.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>(r). The reason is that the density in the outer stellar layers is small and, therefore, its contribution to the radial integral is of minor importance.
</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p41" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">It is obvious from Figure <a href="#S3.F4" title="Figure 4 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> that even on the ZAMS a large fraction of the star would be unscreened against the effects of modified gravity if <span id="S3.p41.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> were as large as 10<span id="S3.p41.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. The effect becomes even more dramatic at the end of the BSG phase where all stellar layers except the very core are unscreened. This is the result of the core-halo density distribution inside BSGs as displayed in Figure <a href="#S3.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> and described eqn. (11) and (12). We note that for <span id="S3.p41.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5<span id="S3.p41.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S3.p41.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> the horizontal orange line in Figure <a href="#S3.F4" title="Figure 4 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> would be 0.3 dex lower and the screening radii slightly larger.</p>
</div>

(19) by</p>

(18) approximates the function <span id="S3.p44.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> equally well. <div id="S3.p48" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Figure <a href="#S3.F5" title="Figure 5 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">5</span></a> shows the ZAMS screening radii r<span id="S3.p48.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> obtained directly from numerical integral of eqn. (4) (corresponding to the red curve in Figure <a href="#S3.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a>) for different stellar masses compared with the approximation of eqn. (21). While there is a 9% systematic offset, the approximation describes the trend with stellar mass very well. The screening radius moves further out when stellar mass increases. This is the result of <span id="S3.p48.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{1\over A}\propto{M\over R}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 0.672em; padding: 0px 0.12em;"><span class="mjx-numerator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0.95em; top: -1.372em;"><span class="mjx-mn" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">1</span></span></span><span class="mjx-denominator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0.95em; bottom: -0.715em;"><span class="mjx-mi" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.519em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">A</span></span></span><span style="border-bottom: 1.3px solid; top: -0.296em; width: 0.672em;" class="mjx-line"></span></span><span style="height: 1.476em; vertical-align: -0.506em;" class="mjx-vsize"></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mo MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">∝</span></span><span class="mjx-texatom MJXc-space3"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 0.885em; padding: 0px 0.12em;"><span class="mjx-numerator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 1.251em; top: -1.389em;"><span class="mjx-mi" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-denominator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 1.251em; bottom: -0.703em;"><span class="mjx-mi" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">R</span></span></span><span style="border-bottom: 1.3px solid; top: -0.296em; width: 0.885em;" class="mjx-line"></span></span><span style="height: 1.48em; vertical-align: -0.497em;" class="mjx-vsize"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and the radius mass relationship of R <span id="S3.p48.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\propto"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">∝</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> M<span id="S3.p48.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{0.57}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0.57</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> on the ZAMS. This leads to <span id="S3.p48.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{1\over A}\propto"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 0.672em; padding: 0px 0.12em;"><span class="mjx-numerator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0.95em; top: -1.372em;"><span class="mjx-mn" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; </div>
<div id="S3.p49" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For BSG stars the ratio of <span id="S3.p49.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{M\over R}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 0.885em; padding: 0px 0.12em;"><span class="mjx-numerator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 1.251em; top: -1.389em;"><span class="mjx-mi" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-denominator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 1.251em; bottom: -0.703em;"><span class="mjx-mi" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">R</span></span></span><span style="border-bottom: 1.3px solid; top: -0.296em; width: 0.885em;" class="mjx-line"></span></span><span style="height: 1.48em; vertical-align: -0.497em;" class="mjx-vsize"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is much smaller, because the stars have expanded significantly, and consequently the screening radii become as small as r<span id="S3.p49.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>/R = 0.06 at the end of the BSG phase as indicated by Figure <a href="#S3.F4" title="Figure 4 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> for the example of 15<span id="S3.p49.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>. For evolutionary tracks with larger initial ZAMS masses r<span id="S3.p49.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>/R can reach values as small as 0.02.</p>

</figcaption>
</figure>
<div id="S3.p50" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The location of the screening radius determines how strong the modification of the gravitational force is in the unscreened region inside the star through the ratio of M(r<span id="S3.p50.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>)/M(r) in eqn. (5). Figure <a href="#S3.F6" title="Figure 6 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">6</span></a> shows the stratification of G(r)/G<span id="S3.p50.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> for selected ZAMS models of different mass. We see that the effects of modified gravity increase with decreasing stellar mass, because the screening radius moves inward according to Figure <a href="#S3.F5" title="Figure 5 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">5</span></a> and eqn. (21) and, therefore, encircles a smaller mass M(r<span id="S3.p50.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{s}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>) relative to the total mass. In the same way modified gravity becomes more important in the evolution of a massive star from the ZAMS to the BSG phase, because the screening radius moves inward during the course of evolution. This is shown in Figure <a href="#S3.F7" title="Figure 7 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">7</span></a> for the example of 15 <span id="S3.p50.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\odot}\;"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">⊙</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-mspace" style="width: 0.278em; height: 0px;"></span></span></span></span></span></span>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p51" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The saturation of G(r)/G<span id="S3.p51.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> towards increasing radii r/R is a consequence of the low density in the outer stellar layers. This means that the incremental increase of the mass M(r) confined within radius r is very small when moving outward and is very close to the total stellar mass. With eq. (5) this leads to the saturation of G(r)/G<span id="S3.p51.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{0}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S3.p52" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Stellar luminosity is affected by the modifications of gravity following eqn. (6). An increase of G(r) also enhances the luminosity and the effect becomes stronger when a larger fraction of the star is unscreened. This explains the qualitative behaviour in Figure <a href="#S3.F2" title="Figure 2 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a>. On the main sequence changes in luminosity are larger at lower masses than at higher masses. They are very small for <span id="S3.p52.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>= 5<span id="S3.p52.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times 10^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">10</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.591em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span id="S3.p52.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3 but increase with <span id="S3.p52.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span id="S3.p52.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, because the screening radius moves inward and G(r) increases. In the BSG phase the increases in luminosity follow the same trend but are significantly larger since a much smaller fraction of the star is unscreened. At <span id="S3.p52.m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 10<span id="S3.p52.m7" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and also with <span id="S3.p52.m8" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1 the effects become extreme and lead to a significant increase of the outer stellar envelopes, in particular, at lower masses. These dramatic changes of the outer stellar structure require extremely small time steps in the numerical calculation of the evolution to accomplish a converged solution. This is the reason why we have stopped the calculations at somewhat higher temperatures at values between 10000K to 15000K.</p>
</div>

<section id="S4" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">4 </span>Modified gravity and flux-weighted gravity</h2>

<div id="S4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Figure <a href="#S3.F8" title="Figure 8 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">8</span></a> displays the spectroscopic Hertzsprung-Russell diagram (sHRD) as introduced by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">Langer and Kudritzki (<a href="#bib.bib36" title="The spectroscopic Hertzsprung-Russell diagram" class="ltx_ref">2014</a>)</cite>, where flux-weighted gravity is plotted versus effective temperature. Again we compare stellar evolution models calculated with Newtonian and modified gravity. The evolutionary tracks of the Newtonian models demonstrate why flux-weighted gravity is a promising distance indicator. It stays roughly constant in the BSG evolutionary phase (where stars become very bright at visual wavelength because of the dependence of bolometric correction on <span id="S4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="T_{\mathrm{eff}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.12em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.12em;">T</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.23em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">e</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>)&nbsp; but at the same time it correlates strongly with luminosity.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The influence of modified gravity is two-fold. Since <span id="S4.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;<span id="S4.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\propto"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">∝</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> GM/L, an increase of G(r) through modified gravity increases <span id="S4.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, whereas the simultaneous increase in luminosity may lead to a decrease of <span id="S4.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. For <span id="S4.p2.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5 <span id="S4.p2.m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; This is still true, when <span id="S4.p2.m9" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is increased to 1, at least at lower masses. For <span id="S4.p2.m10" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5 <span id="S4.F10.m33" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S4.F10.m34" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>; pink: <span id="S4.F10.m35" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3, <span id="S4.F10.m36" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 10<span id="S4.F10.m37" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em;
