violet: <span id="S4.F10.m38" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1, <span id="S4.F10.m39" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5 <span id="S4.F10.m40" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S4.F10.m41" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and 10<span id="S4.F10.m42" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>).</span>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<div id="S4.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The effects of modified gravity encountered in Figure <a href="#S3.F8" title="Figure 8 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">8</span></a> must also be visible in the FGLR of the stellar evolution models. In Figure <a href="#S3.F9" title="Figure 9 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">9</span></a> we have transformed the evolutionary tracks of Figure <a href="#S3.F8" title="Figure 8 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">8</span></a> into diagrams, which displays bolometric magnitude against flux-weighted gravity. We also compare with the observations by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Urbaneja<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib46" title="LMC Blue Supergiant Stars and the Calibration of the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship" class="ltx_ref">2017</a>)</cite> already shown in Figure <a href="#S1.F1" title="Figure 1 ‣ 1 Introduction ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a>. Because of the comparison with BSG observations we restrict the plot of the tracks to the <span id="S4.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="T_{\mathrm{eff}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.12em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.12em;">T</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.23em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">e</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em; padding-right: 0.066em;">f</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;range of BSG.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Before we discuss the influence of modified gravity we need to comment on the comparison of the Newtonian tracks with the observations. At <span id="S4.p4.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">&nbsp;<span id="S4.p4.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\geq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≥</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 1.3</span> we note an offset in <span id="S4.p4.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\mathrm{bol}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.219em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">b</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">o</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">l</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. This offset was already noticed in the work by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Meynet<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib52" title="The flux-weighted gravity-luminosity relationship of blue supergiant stars as a constraint for stellar evolution" class="ltx_ref">2015</a>)</cite> (see their figures 3, 6, and 7), who compared stellar evolution models with observations based on the old FGLR calibration by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib6" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of 24 A Supergiants in the Sculptor Galaxy NGC 300: Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship, Metallicity, and Metallicity Gradient" class="ltx_ref">2008</a>)</cite>. <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Farrell<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib186" title="Impact of binary interaction on the evolution of blue supergiants. The flux-weighted gravity luminosity relationship and extragalactic distance determinations" class="ltx_ref">2019</a>)</cite> compared with the same set of observations but used models which included the effects of binary star evolution. They found a similar offset (see their figures 2 and 3). At this point it is unclear what the physical reason for the offset is. There are many reasons which could affect the evolution of massive stars into the BSG phase such as changes in mass-loss or rotational properties (see <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Meynet<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib52" title="The flux-weighted gravity-luminosity relationship of blue supergiant stars as a constraint for stellar evolution" class="ltx_ref">2015</a></cite>) or changes in the internal angular momentum transport and rotational mixing (see <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Taormina<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib187" title="Toward Early-type Eclipsing Binaries as Extragalactic Milestones. II. NLTE Spectral Analysis and Stellar Parameters of the Detached O-type System OGLE-LMC-ECL-06782 in the LMC" class="ltx_ref">2020</a></cite>). At the same time there is also the possibility that the spectroscopic measurement of BSG flux-weighted gravities are subject to systematic uncertainties. We note that a systematic shift of 0.1 dex in <span id="S4.p4.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp; at higher gravities of the observational data would resolve the problem. Such a shift is, of course, possible. For <span id="S4.p4.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;<span id="S4.p4.m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\leq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 1.3 there is a strong disagreement between between the observed and stellar evolution FGLR slopes. So far, no explanation for this discrepancy has been found. We note, however, that this steep part of the FGLR is of little influence for extragalactic FGLR distance determinations, since most of the extragalactic BSG found are in the range of the higher gravity part.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For a simple straightforward estimate of the potential influence of modified gravity on BSG distances determinations using the FGLR we ignore the discrepancy between observed and model FGLRs and concentrate on the discussion of the systematic differential effects on evolutionary tracks with modified gravity relative to the Newtonian tracks.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The differential effects for <span id="S4.p6.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3 in Figure <a href="#S3.F9" title="Figure 9 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">9</span></a> are small. We fit a straight FGLR curve to the evolutionary tracks assuming <span id="S4.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="M_{\mathrm{bol}}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.081em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.081em;">M</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.219em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">b</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.151em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">o</span></span><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">l</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>= a(<span id="S4.p6.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>-1.5)+b with constant a=3.65 but different b for the three different sets of evolution models. We restrict the fit to the range 2.2 <span id="S4.p6.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\leq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <span id="S4.p6.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\log g_{F}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">log</span></span><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char"></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup MJXc-space1"><span class="mjx-base" style="margin-right: -0.003em;"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em; padding-right: 0.003em;">g</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em; padding-right: 0.106em;">F</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>&nbsp;<span id="S4.p6.m6" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\leq"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">≤</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> 1.2. The difference <span id="S4.p6.m7" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\Delta"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">Δ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>b between modified gravity and the Newtonian models is -0.05 mag and -0.075 mag for <span id="S4.p6.m8" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1/3 and <span id="S4.p6.m9" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5<span id="S4.p6.m10" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S4.p6.m11" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and 10<span id="S4.p6.m12" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, respectively. These differences are comparable to the distances modulus uncertainties obtained from a typical FGLR distance determination. But since the effects are systematic, they may become important, when larger samples of galaxies are used, for instance, to calibrate second order distance indicators. For <span id="S4.p6.m13" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1 the differences are even larger and amount to -0.15 mag for both values of <span id="S4.p6.m14" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. An effect of this size would certainly be important for extragalactic distance determinations. As a consequence, FGLR distances would become larger with increased influence of modified gravity. The changes in distance are comparable to the ones found by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> for Cepheid stars.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">So far, spectroscopic studies of BSG with FGLR measurements have been carried out for nine galaxies (see introduction and Table <a href="#S4.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 4 Modified gravity and flux-weighted gravity ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a>). While this is a relatively small sample, it provides a first opportunity to investigate potential effects of a fifth force on this new stellar distance indicator. As shown by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> the fact that TRGB distances are not affected by modified gravity in the range of <span id="S4.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span id="S4.p7.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> considered here can be used to observationally constrain these parameters. For this purpose it is important to distinguish between galaxies shielded or unscreened against modified gravity. As we already mentioned in the introduction the stars in many galaxies are shielded against modified gravity because of the galaxy gravitational potential or the superimposed potential of neighboring galaxies. However, isolated smaller galaxies are unscreened and here stars would be fully influenced by the fifth force of modified gravity. In those galaxies the FGLR shifts caused by modified gravity would change the distance determinations while TRGB distances would remain unchanged.</p>
</div>

<figcaption class="ltx_caption"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_table">Table 1: </span>Galaxies with <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">observed</span> FGLR and TRGB distance moduli</figcaption></figure>
<div id="S4.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The conditions for screening have been investigated by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Cabré<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib190" title="Astrophysical tests of gravity: a screening map of the nearby universe" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>)</cite> and <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite>. Stars inside a galaxy are shielded against the fifth force, when the absolute value of the galaxy potential is larger than <span id="S4.p8.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{3\over 2}\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mfrac"><span class="mjx-box MJXc-stacked" style="width: 0.495em; padding: 0px 0.12em;"><span class="mjx-numerator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0.7em; top: -1.393em;"><span class="mjx-mn" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">3</span></span></span><span class="mjx-denominator" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0.7em; bottom: -0.665em;"><span class="mjx-mn" style=""><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">2</span></span></span><span style="border-bottom: 1.3px solid; top: -0.296em; width: 0.495em;" class="mjx-line"></span></span><span style="height: 1.456em; vertical-align: -0.47em;" class="mjx-vsize"></span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. This is the case of internal screening. As shown by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Jain<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib176" title="Astrophysical Tests of Modified Gravity: Constraints from Distance Indicators in the Nearby Universe" class="ltx_ref">2013</a>)</cite> the observed maximal rotational velocity v<span id="S4.p8.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{m}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> can be used to estimate the potential. This leads to the condition 2<span id="S4.p8.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S4.p8.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>(v<span id="S4.p8.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{m}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; The condition for external screening can be approximated by the addition of the point source potentials of all neighbor galaxies within a radius <span id="S4.p8.m10" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\lambda_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Mpc. For the calculation of galaxy screening in the nearby universe <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Cabré<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib190" title="Astrophysical tests of gravity: a screening map of the nearby universe" class="ltx_ref">2012</a>)</cite> provide two galaxy catalogues on their website based on the work by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Karachentsev<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib192" title="A Catalog of Neighboring Galaxies" class="ltx_ref">2004</a>)</cite> and <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Lavaux and Hudson (<a href="#bib.bib191" title="The 2M++ galaxy redshift catalogue" class="ltx_ref">2011</a>)</cite>, which we have utilized. (We have updated some of the values of v<span id="S4.p8.m20" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{m}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and M<span id="S4.p8.m21" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}_{i}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">i</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> taking into account more recent work).</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Applying the screening conditions as outlined we find that three galaxies of our sample (M81, M83, and M33) are screened against a fifth force characterized by <span id="S4.p9.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5<span id="S4.p9.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S4.p9.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">7</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. The remaining galaxies (NGC3621, NGC300, NGC 55, NGC 3109, IC 1613, WLM) are unscreened. For <span id="S4.p9.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 10<span id="S4.p9.m5" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-6}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: 0.513em; padding-left: 0px; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.298em; padding-bottom: 0.446em;">−</span></span><span class="mjx-mn"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.372em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">6</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> M33 and M83 become unscreened as well.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p10" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We have used the FGLR calibration of eqn. (1) and (2) to re-determine distances to the eight galaxies mentioned in the introduction. We also determined an FGLR distance to NGC 300 using the spectroscopic results by <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Kudritzki<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> (<a href="#bib.bib6" title="Quantitative Spectroscopy of 24 A Supergiants in the Sculptor Galaxy NGC 300: Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship, Metallicity, and Metallicity Gradient" class="ltx_ref">2008</a>)</cite><span>. All nine galaxies also have accurate TRGB distances determined consistently in a homogeneous way and published in the EDD database (<a href="http://edd.ifa.hawaii.edu">http://edd.ifa.hawaii.edu</a>, see </span><cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citet">Tully<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib188" title="The Extragalactic Distance Database" class="ltx_ref">2009</a></cite>). A subset of four galaxies (M81, NGC55, NGC300, NGC3109) has also TRGB distances determined by the ANGST project <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_citep">(Dalcanton<span class="ltx_text ltx_bib_etal"> et al.</span> <a href="#bib.bib189" title="The ACS Nearby Galaxy Survey Treasury" class="ltx_ref">2009</a>)</cite>. For those we use the mean between EDD and ANGST. The FGLR and TRGB distance moduli for the nine galaxies are given in Table <a href="#S4.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 4 Modified gravity and flux-weighted gravity ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a>.</p>
</div>

padding-bottom: 0.372em;">±</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>0.135 for the one remaining shielded galaxy M81.</p>
</div>
<div id="S4.p12" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">According to the differential effects of our fits to the stellar evolution FGLRs of Figure <a href="#S3.F9" title="Figure 9 ‣ 3 Modified Gravity and Massive Star Evolution ‣ Modified Gravity and the Flux-weighted Gravity-Luminosity Relationship of Blue Supergiant Stars" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">9</span></a> we would expect <span id="S4.p12.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\overline{\Delta}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-munderover"><span class="mjx-stack"><span class="mjx-over" style="font-size: 70.7%; height: 0.096em; padding-bottom: 0.283em; padding-top: 0.141em;"><span class="mjx-mo" style="vertical-align: top;"><span class="mjx-delim-h"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.301em; However, the values obtained for the unscreened samples are positive and the differences are larger than 2.7 standard deviations for <span id="S4.p12.m8" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1. Formally, adopting a Gaussian distribution for <span id="S4.p12.m9" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\overline{\Delta}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-munderover"><span class="mjx-stack"><span class="mjx-over" style="font-size: 70.7%; height: 0.096em; padding-bottom: 0.283em; padding-top: 0.141em;"><span class="mjx-mo" style="vertical-align: top;"><span class="mjx-delim-h"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.301em; padding-bottom: 0.833em; margin: 0px -0.07em 0px -0.069em;">¯</span><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.301em; padding-bottom: 0.833em; letter-spacing: -0.315em; margin: 0px 0.068em 0px -0.207em;">¯¯¯</span><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.301em; padding-bottom: 0.833em; margin-right: -0.07em; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-top: 0px;">¯</span></span></span></span><span class="mjx-op"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">Δ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> the probability of <span id="S4.p12.m10" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">α</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 1 being consistent with our measurement is smaller than 4%. The probabilities for <span id="S4.p12.m11" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\alpha_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; </div>
<div id="S4.p13" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We note that by calculating probabilities in this way we make the assumption that the distance moduli obtained by the TRGB and FGLR method, respectively, are not affected by systematic effects based on their calibrations. If, for instance, <span id="S4.p13.m1" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\Delta"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.446em; padding-bottom: 0.372em;">Δ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span> would have a systematic positive offset caused by calibration systematics, this would compensate for the negative shifts induced by modified gravity in the case of unscreened galaxies. Of course, by including the screened samples in our consideration we can study the differential effects between screened and unscreened galaxies. Unfortunately, the number of screened galaxies is small and the means are more uncertain. For <span id="S4.p13.m2" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\chi_{c}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.519em;">χ</span></span></span><span class="mjx-sub" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.212em; padding-right: 0.071em;"><span class="mjx-texatom" style=""><span class="mjx-mrow"><span class="mjx-mi"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-math-I" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">c</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> = 5<span id="S4.p13.m3" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="\times"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-mo"><span class="mjx-char MJXc-TeX-main-R" style="padding-top: 0.225em; padding-bottom: 0.298em;">×</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>10<span id="S4.p13.m4" class="ltx_Math"><span class="mjpage"><span class="mjx-chtml"><span class="mjx-math" aria-label="{}^{-7}"><span class="mjx-mrow" aria-hidden="true"><span class="mjx-msubsup"><span class="mjx-base"><span class="mjx-texatom"><span class="mjx-mrow"></span></span></span><span class="mjx-sup" style="font-size: 70.7%;
